# Multiple Filters | Proxyman

[](https://docs.proxyman.com/advanced-features/multiple-filters#id-1.-whats-it)

1\. What's it?


---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

From build 2.22.0+, you can combine many filters at one time.

*   Easily and quickly filter the request/response with complex filtered criteria
    
*   Persist your last filter configs
    
*   Handy Shortcuts
    
*   Various Filters: URL, Request Header, Response Header, Body, Status Code, Method, Color, and Comment
    
*   Combine with AND / OR all filters
    

![](https://docs.proxyman.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F1856518738-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-legacy-files%2Fo%2Fassets%252F-LlPt_6BePnJ3oK3saP1%252F-MWwDlZECbkfQm4piN0i%252F-MWwF9FpSzI60WypwUFV%252FExYFSpHUcAYVbKp.jpeg%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D07ea3c4a-6e9f-4e68-bf31-9773f3fdbea3&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=298f70fe&sv=2)

Mulitple Filter

### 

[](https://docs.proxyman.com/advanced-features/multiple-filters#id-2.-shortcut)

2\. Shortcut

Shortcut

Description

⌘F

Display the filter and focus on the last one

⌘N

Clone new filter

⇧⌘N

Remove current Filter

⌘↑

Focus on the previous filter

⌘↓

Focus on the next filter

ESC

Dismiss the filter

Proxyman limit the maximum filters is 10

For a Freemium version, it's limited at 2

# Publish to Gist | Proxyman

[](https://docs.proxyman.com/advanced-features/publish-to-gist#id-1.-whats-it)

1\. What's it?


--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

From Proxyman 2.28.0+, the developer can publish Request/Response data to Github Gist.

*   Proxyman requires "Read/Write Gist" permission in order to publish a Gist on the user's behalf.
    
*   If it's the first time, Proxyman will prompt a Github Authorization Page.
    

[](https://docs.proxyman.com/advanced-features/publish-to-gist#id-2.-benefit)

2\. Benefit


----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

*   **Instantly** create a Gist from selected Request/Response that you can **quickly** share with your colleagues.
    
*   Support Private and Private Gist.
    
*   Only requires **"Read/Write Gist"** permission. No request for Email/Username/...
    
*   The Github Access Token is securely stored in User Keychain.
    

Here is how the Gist looks like: [https://gist.github.com/NghiaTranUIT/e116a60e286c917a5cbfd61aff32194c](https://gist.github.com/NghiaTranUIT/e116a60e286c917a5cbfd61aff32194c)

![](https://docs.proxyman.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F1856518738-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-legacy-files%2Fo%2Fassets%252F-LlPt_6BePnJ3oK3saP1%252F-Mb0e6XewuPDovrJZpyY%252F-Mb0fph-a8B9yc8jRme-%252FScreen%2520Shot%25202021-05-31%2520at%252015.54.36.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D37a1ef5a-e622-4dfd-8a46-9d03b27f95c2&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=356a715b&sv=2)

[](https://docs.proxyman.com/advanced-features/publish-to-gist#id-3.-how-to-use)

3\. How to use


----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

1.  Select your request on the main Table View
    
2.  Right-Click to display a Menu Context -> Export -> Publish To Gist...
    

![](https://docs.proxyman.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F1856518738-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-legacy-files%2Fo%2Fassets%252F-LlPt_6BePnJ3oK3saP1%252F-Mb0e6XewuPDovrJZpyY%252F-Mb0hNx-X6tXs5aGbMQJ%252FScreen_Shot_2021-05-31_at_15_54_31.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Da2748fe6-8d4b-45e2-ba2d-727dbd6fc58f&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=b58e9aca&sv=2)

# Reverse Proxy | Proxyman

### 

[](https://docs.proxyman.com/advanced-features/reverse-proxy#id-1.-whats-it)

1\. What's it?

Reverse Proxy would create a **local WebServer** that transparently proxies your traffic to a remote server. By doing this way, Proxyman can capture and log your traffic.

Reverse Proxy is useful when you are working on a client that doesn't support HTTP/HTTPS Proxy or the HTTP Proxy config is too complicated.

For instance, the majority of Command-Line apps would not respect the system HTTP/HTTPS proxies, so Proxyman could not capture its traffic. To resolve it, you have to either:

*   Explicitly config an HTTP/HTTPS Proxy. It's complicated and depends on the network library you are using. Check out this [troubleshooting](https://docs.proxyman.com/troubleshooting/couldnt-see-any-requests-from-3rd-party-network-libraries)
     to know further.
    
*   Use Reverse Proxy.
    

Reverse Proxy is available on Proxyman 2.29.0+.

### 

[](https://docs.proxyman.com/advanced-features/reverse-proxy#id-2.-benefit)

2\. Benefit

*   Reverse Proxy feature: You can connect to Proxyman local WebServer, and it will forward your traffic to the remote host. No need to set up an HTTP/HTTPS Proxy on your client.
    
*   Import Reverse Proxy Setting from Charles Proxy.
    
*   Preserve Host in Header.
    
*   Automatically select the available port when creating a new entry.
    
*   Able to use Breakpoint, Map Local, Scripting for Reverse Proxy traffic 💯.
    

### 

[](https://docs.proxyman.com/advanced-features/reverse-proxy#id-3.-how-to-use)

3\. How to use

1.  Access Reverse Proxy tool from Tools Menu -> Reverse Proxy
    
2.  Create a new entry by entering a Remote Host and Remote Port. For the Local port, Proxyman would select automatically. You can change to a different port, but it must be available.
    
3.  Save.
    
4.  On your client application, change the URL to http://localhost:<local\_port> (e.g. http://localhost:10000)
    
5.  Make a request and inspect the traffic from the Proxyman app.
    

![](https://docs.proxyman.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F1856518738-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-legacy-files%2Fo%2Fassets%252F-LlPt_6BePnJ3oK3saP1%252F-MdAERP18CoGcrMNbD3Y%252F-MdAGoxm_NUHCiSvMu7x%252FScreen%2520Shot%25202021-06-26%2520at%252017.05.42.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D7a106ec6-f42f-498f-b509-d3ce9f5db1ed&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=e0b4330c&sv=2)

Reverse Proxy Tool

![](https://docs.proxyman.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F1856518738-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-legacy-files%2Fo%2Fassets%252F-LlPt_6BePnJ3oK3saP1%252F-MdAGreiZFaAKsQfN_vv%252F-MdAGunvGvvXWx91ro2J%252FScreen%2520Shot%25202021-06-26%2520at%252017.05.45.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D20216e7d-ea9b-4c41-b88d-85d96c71c148&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=d714e1bf&sv=2)

Create new Reverse Proxy Entry

Proxyman would perform SSL Handshake to your Remote Server if the port is 443. Otherwise, it considers as a normal HTTP WebServer.

**Preserve Host in Header Fields** allows you to preserve the original Host value. You should use it with caution because your remote server can reject the request due to a mismatched Host Value.

[PreviousPublish to Gist](https://docs.proxyman.com/advanced-features/publish-to-gist)
[NextCode Generator](https://docs.proxyman.com/advanced-features/code-generator)

*   [2\. Benefit](https://docs.proxyman.com/advanced-features/reverse-proxy#id-2.-benefit)

# Repeat | Proxyman

### 

[](https://docs.proxyman.com/advanced-features/repeat#id-1.-whats-it)

1\. What's it?

Repeat tool is a useful tool for quickly making a new HTTP request with the same HTTP Header and Body for seeing the new response without changing from your browsers or clients.

### 

[](https://docs.proxyman.com/advanced-features/repeat#id-2.-whats-it-for)

2\. What's it for?

*   Quickly make an HTTP/HTTPS Request for testing the newest response from the server.
    
*   It's useful for developers to test the change of the server without repeating the request manually.
    

Repeat tool only supports HTTP/HTTPS Requests. Repeat on WS/WSS traffic might be failed.

Repeated requests can be modified by the Breakpoint, Map Local, and Scripting tool if it matches any rules.

### 

[](https://docs.proxyman.com/advanced-features/repeat#id-3.-how-to-use)

3\. How to use

*   Right-Click on a single or multiple Request(s) -> **Repeat**
    

![](https://docs.proxyman.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F1856518738-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252F-LlPt_6BePnJ3oK3saP1%252Fuploads%252FIqaM1b6s9R5KYortG3rV%252FScreen_Shot_2022-06-23_at_14_49_23.jpg%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D930e9a0a-5e71-47bd-809f-462072ea3755&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=c713e2e8&sv=2)

Quickly repeat the current requests

⌘ ⏎ : Repeat the current selected request.

### 

[](https://docs.proxyman.com/advanced-features/repeat#id-4.-settings)

4\. Settings

*   **Request Timeout**: In Setting -> Tools Tab -> Request Timeout: Define a second that the Request will timeout. Use 0 to disable it. Available on Proxyman 4.13.0 or later
    

[PreviousCommand Palette](https://docs.proxyman.com/basic-features/command-palette)
[NextEdit & Repeat](https://docs.proxyman.com/advanced-features/edit-and-repeat)

Last updated 1 year ago

# Map Local (Directory) | Proxyman

[](https://docs.proxyman.com/advanced-features/map-local-directory#id-1.-whats-it)

1\. What's it?


------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

It's a handy tool to map a matched requests to local files on a selected Directory. If the local files doesn't exist, it will serve from the real server.

If you would like to map a Local File, let check out the Map Local (File) page

[Map Local (File)](https://docs.proxyman.com/advanced-features/map-local)

[](https://docs.proxyman.com/advanced-features/map-local-directory#id-2.-how-to-use)

2\. How to use


--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

### 

[](https://docs.proxyman.com/advanced-features/map-local-directory#id-2.1-map-a-path-and-its-subdirectories)

2.1 Map a path and its subdirectories

`api.proxyman.io/build/v1/*` => All sub-paths after `/v1/` will map to a selected directory.

For instance, we select `~/desktop/my_folder` as the local directory

Real URL

Resolved Local Path

http://api.proxyman.io/build/v1/index.html

~/desktop/my\_folder/index.html

http://api.proxyman.io/build/v1/js/main.js

~/desktop/my\_folder/js/main.js

#### 

[](https://docs.proxyman.com/advanced-features/map-local-directory#how-to-config)

How to config

Rule

How to use

Examples

Wildcard

*   Check ON "Include subpaths" checkbox
    
*   Or use /\* at the end of the URL
    

*   api.proxyman.io/build/v1/ (Check ON)
    
*   api.proxyman.io/build/v1/\*
    

Regex

*   Use (.\*) at the end
    

*   https:\\/\\/api.proxyman.io\\/build\\/v1\\/(.\*)
    
*   https:\\/\\/api.proxyman.io\\/build\\/v1\\/(.\*.css)
    

Make sure you use `()` group Regex operator to tell Proxyman where to map

### 

[](https://docs.proxyman.com/advanced-features/map-local-directory#id-2.2-map-entire-host)

2.2 Map Entire Host

`api.proxyman.io/*` => All sub-paths will map to a selected directory.

For instance, we select `~/desktop/my_folder` as the local directory

Real URL

Resolved Local Path

http://api.proxyman.io/build/v1/index.html

~/desktop/my\_folder/build/v1/index.html

http://api.proxyman.io/build/v1/js/main.js

~/desktop/my\_folder/build/v1/js/main.js

#### 

[](https://docs.proxyman.com/advanced-features/map-local-directory#how-to-config-1)

How to config

Rule

How to use

Examples

Wildcard

*   Leave the path blank
    

*   api.proxyman.io
    

Regex

*   Use single path that contains (.\*) at the end
    

*   https:\\/\\/api.proxyman.io\\/(.\*)
    
*   https:\\/\\/api.proxyman.io\\/(\*.html)
    

[](https://docs.proxyman.com/advanced-features/map-local-directory#id-3.-map-local-directoy-with-scripting-tool)

3\. Map Local Directoy with Scripting Tool ✅


------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

If you would like to do Map Local Directory with **complicated rules,** you might check out [Scripting](https://docs.proxyman.com/scripting/script#1-whats-it)
 since it's easier to achieve the same result.

Please check out our [Snippet Code](https://docs.proxyman.com/scripting/snippet-code#2-common-on-request-and-response)
 to understand how to map a local file with Javascript Code.

[PreviousMap Local (File)](https://docs.proxyman.com/advanced-features/map-local)
[NextMap Remote](https://docs.proxyman.com/advanced-features/map-remote)

Last updated 4 years ago

*   [1\. What's it?](https://docs.proxyman.com/advanced-features/map-local-directory#id-1.-whats-it)
    
*   [2\. How to use](https://docs.proxyman.com/advanced-features/map-local-directory#id-2.-how-to-use)

# Charles Proxy Converter | Proxyman

[](https://docs.proxyman.com/advanced-features/charles-proxy-converter#id-1.-whats-it)

1\. What's it?


----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Proxyman is capable of converting and reading the `chls` files from Charles Proxy app to `har` format that Proxyman can understand.

It requires that Charles Proxy beis already installed in order to convert `chls` files

You can manually convert the files from the File menu -> Convert -> `chls` to `har`

![](https://docs.proxyman.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F1856518738-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-legacy-files%2Fo%2Fassets%252F-LlPt_6BePnJ3oK3saP1%252F-M6PIQiDj7p2umCK6D5Y%252F-M6PIce9rkDFwLNTFfBY%252FScreen%2520Shot%25202020-05-03%2520at%252018.31.39.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Dbdb9ae4f-9a63-4eb0-a199-cd50b532cced&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=f0a214cb&sv=2)

[](https://docs.proxyman.com/advanced-features/charles-proxy-converter#id-2.-how-does-it-work)

2\. How does it work?


-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

In general, Proxyman uses [Convert CLI from Charles Proxy](https://www.charlesproxy.com/documentation/tools/command-line-tools/)
 to convert .chls to .har, which Proxyman can understand.

1.  As soon as you open `chls` file, Proxyman tries to find the Charles Proxy app, which has a bundle ID is
    
    `com.xk72.Charles`
    
2.  Convert by using the convert command
    

3\. The output is `har` formatted in your Desktop directory

[](https://docs.proxyman.com/advanced-features/charles-proxy-converter#id-3.-how-to-use)

3\. How to use?


-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

There are several ways to open `chls` files:

*   Open the `chls` file directly (Double-Click on the file, or Open With from Finder app)
    
*   Drag and drop the file to the Proxyman app
    
*   File -> Open and select `chls` files
    

[PreviousAllow List](https://docs.proxyman.com/advanced-features/whitelist)
[NextCustom Certificates](https://docs.proxyman.com/advanced-features/custom-certificates)

Last updated 3 months ago

*   [1\. What's it?](https://docs.proxyman.com/advanced-features/charles-proxy-converter#id-1.-whats-it)
    
*   [2\. How does it work?](https://docs.proxyman.com/advanced-features/charles-proxy-converter#id-2.-how-does-it-work)
    
*   [3\. How to use?](https://docs.proxyman.com/advanced-features/charles-proxy-converter#id-3.-how-to-use)
    

Copy

    $ ./Applications/Charles.app/Contents/MacOS/Charles convert ~/Desktop/input.chls ~/Desktop/output.har

# Protobuf | Proxyman

### 

[](https://docs.proxyman.com/advanced-features/protobuf#id-1.-protocol-buffer)

1\. Protocol Buffer

From [Protobuf's Google](https://developers.google.com/protocol-buffers/)
, Protocol buffers are Google's language-neutral, platform-neutral, extensible mechanism for serializing structured data – think XML, but smaller, faster, and simpler.

You define how you want your data to be structured once, then you can use special generated source code to easily write and read your structured data to and from a variety of data streams and using a variety of languages.

Proxyman is capable of **reading** a Protobuf Binary and parsing to **JSON Format** with given Protobuf File Descriptors.

![](https://docs.proxyman.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F1856518738-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-legacy-files%2Fo%2Fassets%252F-LlPt_6BePnJ3oK3saP1%252F-M5lixcwWeMPWwvY2whW%252F-M5lkc_hSq_6DhDF6Az5%252FScreen_Shot_2020-04-25_at_21_32_54.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D70cdd7c2-5c07-49e7-99fc-84fb0d94bfa8&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=d83a495f&sv=2)

Parse protobuf request with File Descriptor

### 

[](https://docs.proxyman.com/advanced-features/protobuf#id-2.-protobuf-file-descriptor-.desc)

2\. Protobuf File Descriptor (\*.desc)

Proxyman requires File Descriptor (\*.desc) to properly parse the Protobuf Data.

There are various ways to get the File Descriptor:

#### 

[](https://docs.proxyman.com/advanced-features/protobuf#id-1.-ask-your-colleagues)

1\. Ask your colleagues.

If your company is using Protobuf, it's a high chance that your colleagues have already had this file, especially the Backend and Frontend teams.

It might be one or multiple descriptor files.

#### 

[](https://docs.proxyman.com/advanced-features/protobuf#id-2.-generate-from-.proto-file)

2\. Generate from \*.proto file

If you have a bunch of \*.proto files, you can simply generate 1 single \*.desc file by using the following command line.

Once you have the Descriptor File, you can import them to Proxyman:

*   Proxyman -> Tools Menu -> Protobuf Schema
    
*   Click on the + button and select the **output.desc** file
    

Proxyman 3.6.0+ only accepts **File Descriptor (\*.desc)** for better Protobuf parsing.

If you have **\*.proto** files, you can convert them to **\*.desc**. Please check out the next section.

Proxyman automatically imports all common types from **Google Protobuf**, such as Timestamp, Struct, Value, Enum, Method, etc.

Proxyman supports both **proto2** and **proto3** syntax. [Read more](https://developers.google.com/protocol-buffers/docs/proto3)

### 

[](https://docs.proxyman.com/advanced-features/protobuf#id-3.-protobuf-config)

3\. Protobuf Config

Before using Protobuf, you have to config which Message Type should be used to parse the Protobuf data.

The following table describes which config are:

Name

Description

Schema

Add `.desc` file if need

Message Type

The Class name of the root object in Protobuf binary. **Must include Package name**

Payload Type: **Auto**

Auto detect if the Protobuf Binary is encoding as a Single Message or [Delimited Message](https://developers.google.com/protocol-buffers/docs/techniques#streaming)

Payload Type: **Single Message**

Single Mesage in a Protobuf Binary

Payload Type: **Delimited Message**

Multiple Messages in a Protobuf Binary (Length-Prefix)

![](https://docs.proxyman.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F1856518738-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-legacy-files%2Fo%2Fassets%252F-LlPt_6BePnJ3oK3saP1%252F-M5lixcwWeMPWwvY2whW%252F-M5lmAlPcvbTehjdCiFz%252FScreen%2520Shot%25202020-04-25%2520at%252021.40.16.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D8ee4e3fe-b1e9-40c4-8a16-f9b036c7b2ba&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=66bfaf39&sv=2)

Add Message Type to particular requests

### 

[](https://docs.proxyman.com/advanced-features/protobuf#id-4.-how-to-use)

4\. How to use?

There are **two** ways to parse Protobuf properly with qualified name fields:

*   Define Protobuf Rules
    
*   Read from Content-Type Header
    

#### 

[](https://docs.proxyman.com/advanced-features/protobuf#id-4.1-define-protobuf-rule)

4.1 Define Protobuf Rule

1.  Make a request, which has `Content-Type: application/x-protobuf` or `Content-Type: application/protobuf`
    
2.  You can see the Warning that Proxyman couldn't parse properly due to the absence of Message Type. Click Add to open Protobuf Settings
    

![](https://docs.proxyman.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F1856518738-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-legacy-files%2Fo%2Fassets%252F-LlPt_6BePnJ3oK3saP1%252F-M5lnvriZFMegQHaQMbz%252F-M5lq38TdKPlCYQk1JvO%252FScreen_Shot_2020-04-25_at_21_56_19.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Dfe738ee8-808e-4032-ac8c-23fec9123fe2&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=3b5f53b4&sv=2)

Missing Message Type

3\. Add Schema and fill Message type and Payload Type:

*   Right Click on the Protobuf Request -> Tools -> Protobuf
    
*   Select which Message Type for this request (Add Desc file if need)
    

![](https://docs.proxyman.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F1856518738-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-legacy-files%2Fo%2Fassets%252F-LlPt_6BePnJ3oK3saP1%252F-M5lixcwWeMPWwvY2whW%252F-M5lmAlPcvbTehjdCiFz%252FScreen%2520Shot%25202020-04-25%2520at%252021.40.16.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D8ee4e3fe-b1e9-40c4-8a16-f9b036c7b2ba&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=66bfaf39&sv=2)

4\. Click Add and see qualified JSON Format

![](https://docs.proxyman.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F1856518738-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-legacy-files%2Fo%2Fassets%252F-LlPt_6BePnJ3oK3saP1%252F-M5lnvriZFMegQHaQMbz%252F-M5lsSsNQf3WDg0JIvmX%252FScreen%2520Shot%25202020-04-25%2520at%252022.08.07.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3De7b4f811-5fb5-4e03-beda-5ddd696abab2&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=93d88e30&sv=2)

#### 

[](https://docs.proxyman.com/advanced-features/protobuf#id-4.2-read-from-content-type-header)

4.2 Read from Content-Type Header

You can **dynamically** provide the Protobuf Config from `Content-Type`

For example: Your `Content-Type` in the Request or Response might look like:

`Content-Type: application/x-protobuf; messageType="tutorial.Address"; delimited=true`

`Content-Type: application/x-protobuf; messageType="com.proxyman.User"; delimited=false`

To specify that the Protobuf Body this MessageType and the payload encoding.

### 

[](https://docs.proxyman.com/advanced-features/protobuf#id-5.-troubleshooting)

5\. Troubleshooting

#### 

[](https://docs.proxyman.com/advanced-features/protobuf#id-5.1-some-name-fields-are-missing)

5.1 Some name fields are missing

There is a situation where some field names are absent because the field name definition is not included in your Protobuf File Descriptor. It might be your descriptor is out of date.

**Solution**:

*   Remove old Protobuf Schema and Add the latest descriptor file from your server.
    
*   If you're using Proxyman 3.5.2 and older, please update to Proxyman 3.6.0 or later. Then, use File Descriptor (\*.desc) for better results.
    

[PreviousSave Session](https://docs.proxyman.com/advanced-features/save-session)
[NextWebSocket](https://docs.proxyman.com/advanced-features/websocket)

Last updated 10 months ago

*   [1\. Protocol Buffer](https://docs.proxyman.com/advanced-features/protobuf#id-1.-protocol-buffer)
    
*   [2\. Protobuf File Descriptor (\*.desc)](https://docs.proxyman.com/advanced-features/protobuf#id-2.-protobuf-file-descriptor-.desc)
    
*   [3\. Protobuf Config](https://docs.proxyman.com/advanced-features/protobuf#id-3.-protobuf-config)
    
*   [4\. How to use?](https://docs.proxyman.com/advanced-features/protobuf#id-4.-how-to-use)
    
*   [5\. Troubleshooting](https://docs.proxyman.com/advanced-features/protobuf#id-5.-troubleshooting)
    

Copy

    # Install protobuf cli if need
    brew install protobuf
    
    # Create `input` folder on the Desktop
    # Copy all proto files to the `input` folder
    
    # Generate 1 descriptor file with multiple proto files
    protoc --descriptor_set_out=output.desc --include_imports -I=/Users/<your_name>/Desktop/input /Users/<your_name>/Desktop/input/*.proto
    
    # Done
    # output.desc

# Code Generator | Proxyman

[](https://docs.proxyman.com/advanced-features/code-generator#id-1.-whats-it)

1\. What's it?


-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Code Generator is a useful tool that helps you automatically generate your HTTP/HTTPS Requests for particular code languages.

The following table will list all supported languages:

*   cURL
    
*   HTTPie
    
*   HAR
    
*   Postman Collection 2
    
*   Axios
    
*   Go
    
*   Java + HTTPClient
    
*   Javascript + jQuery
    
*   Node + HTTP
    
*   Node + Fetch
    
*   Python + Request
    
*   Objective-C + NSURLSession
    
*   Swift + Alamofire 5
    
*   Swift + Moya
    
*   Swift + URLSession
    

![](https://docs.proxyman.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F1856518738-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-legacy-files%2Fo%2Fassets%252F-LlPt_6BePnJ3oK3saP1%252F-Mi4cbS8HHJFoufQOywH%252F-Mi4e7knCxyCTQxI4GiT%252Fcode-generator.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D653f2edc-7ea3-42ad-af12-40ec9ff118ac&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=a40c87fd&sv=2)

Generate Swift + Alamofire 5 Code

[](https://docs.proxyman.com/advanced-features/code-generator#id-2.-how-to-open-the-code-generator-tab)

2\. How to open the Code Generator Tab?


----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

1.  On the Request Panel Tab -> Click on the "+" Button
    
2.  New Windows appears -> Click on the "Code Generator" checkbox
    

![](https://docs.proxyman.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F1856518738-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252F-LlPt_6BePnJ3oK3saP1%252Fuploads%252Fq6alY9uza5DrvoWQAFSs%252FCleanShot%25202025-01-29%2520at%25203%25E2%2580%25AF.44.21%25402x.jpg%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Ddbcb763d-c629-420c-8c6c-990e9ec759de&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=85149a24&sv=2)

How to open the Code Generator Tab

*   New Tab will add to the Request Panel -> Select any language to show the code
    

[](https://docs.proxyman.com/advanced-features/code-generator#id-3.-missing-your-favorite-library)

3\. Missing your favorite library?


------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

If you cannot find your library, you can:

*   Create a [Ticket](https://github.com/ProxymanApp/Proxyman/issues)
     on Github.
    
*   Fork [Code-Generator-Plugin Repository](https://github.com/ProxymanApp/code-generator-plugin)
     and open a PR. We appreciate your contribution 🙇‍♂️

# Network Conditions | Proxyman

### 

[](https://docs.proxyman.com/advanced-features/network-throttling#id-1.-whats-it)

1\. What's it?

Network Conditions (Network Throttling) v1 allows developers to simulate adverse networking environments. Proxyman provides various preset profiles:

Profile

Description

100% Lost connection

100 % lost all connection

Very Bad Network

Download/Upload: < 1mbps

Slow Network

Download/Upload: 5-10 mbps

Medium Network

Download/Upload: 10-20 mbps

2G (EDGE)

Download: <240kbps, Upload <200kbps

3G

Download: <780kbps, Upload <300kbps

4G (LTE)

Download: 30-50mbps, Upload 5-10mbps

Wi-Fi

Download: 25-40mbps, Upload 15-30mbps

Wi-Fi 802.11ac

Download: 150-250mbps, Upload 70-100mbps

### 

[](https://docs.proxyman.com/advanced-features/network-throttling#id-2.-benefit)

2\. Benefit?

*   Various preset profiles: 3G, 4G, Wifi, Bad/Medium Network, etc.
    
*   Help developers to simulate various network conditions (Download/Upload Bandwidth, Packets Dropped rate, delay).
    
*   Easier to test your app under a particular network condition.
    
*   Apply for **system-Wide** or **certain domains**.
    

Network Conditions v1 does not allow you to customize a profile. We will implement it in v2.

To better simulate the real-life, the download/upload bandwidth is not fixed, it might randomize in a given range.

### 

[](https://docs.proxyman.com/advanced-features/network-throttling#id-3.-how-to-use-it)

3\. How to use it?

You can access the feature by navigating to Tool -> Network Condition (CMD+SHIFT+J) or access from the right-menu context.

![](https://docs.proxyman.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F1856518738-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-legacy-files%2Fo%2Fassets%252F-LlPt_6BePnJ3oK3saP1%252F-MVit2xH7yEC5FgKyj2f%252F-MVit7lBYfPWRzmass9F%252FScreen%2520Shot%25202021-03-14%2520at%252009.59.23.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D389ae2fd-021d-4250-9a9b-49ac30e57392&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=240090ec&sv=2)

Set Network Condition for particular domain

### 

[](https://docs.proxyman.com/advanced-features/network-throttling#id-4.-alternative)

4\. Alternative

*   Network Link Conditions for macOS: [https://nshipster.com/network-link-conditioner/](https://nshipster.com/network-link-conditioner/)

# DNS Spoofing | Proxyman

[](https://docs.proxyman.com/advanced-features/dns-spoofing#id-1.-whats-it)

1\. What's it?


-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

DNS Spoofing allows developers:

*   Provide a custom DNS for particular domains
    
*   Able to map from a domain to different domains
    

![](https://docs.proxyman.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F1856518738-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252F-LlPt_6BePnJ3oK3saP1%252Fuploads%252FMaaOHZJCNK1UeU8jFG09%252F1.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D47fa3a35-58cf-4be5-b7d2-8cd39a172589&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=293eb39b&sv=2)

DNS Spoofing

[](https://docs.proxyman.com/advanced-features/dns-spoofing#id-2.-what-is-different-with-map-remote)

2\. What is different with Map Remote?


------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

DNS Spoofing is different than Map Remote by:

*   The \`Host\` in the Request Header doesn't change
    
*   The URL doesn't change
    

On the other hand, Map Remote allows you to change the Host Header and the mapped URL.

[](https://docs.proxyman.com/advanced-features/dns-spoofing#id-3.-how-to-use-it)

3\. How to use it?


--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

1.  Simply create a new rule by opening the Tools Menu -> DNS Spoofing
    
2.  Create new Rule with the Host name and Remote Address
    
3.  Done ✅
    

[PreviousAccess Control](https://docs.proxyman.com/advanced-features/access-control)
[NextSOCKS Proxy](https://docs.proxyman.com/advanced-features/socks-proxy)

Last updated 2 years ago

*   [1\. What's it?](https://docs.proxyman.com/advanced-features/dns-spoofing#id-1.-whats-it)
    
*   [2\. What is different with Map Remote?](https://docs.proxyman.com/advanced-features/dns-spoofing#id-2.-what-is-different-with-map-remote)
    
*   [3\. How to use it?](https://docs.proxyman.com/advanced-features/dns-spoofing#id-3.-how-to-use-it)

# Diff | Proxyman

### 

[](https://docs.proxyman.com/advanced-features/diff#id-1.-whats-it)

1\. What's it?

During using Proxyman, you might face the situation to find the difference between requests and responses. The Diff tool would help you to:

*   Diff two Requests or Response, include the URL, Method, Status Code, Headers, and the Text-based body.
    
*   Render as Side-by-Side or Unified.
    
*   Light and Dark Theme.
    
*   Export as a unified file.
    
*   Open the diff by 3rd-party applications, such as FileMerge.
    
*   Highlight and add comments.
    

This feature is only available for macOS 11.2 and later.

### 

[](https://docs.proxyman.com/advanced-features/diff#id-2.-how-to-use-it)

2\. How to use it?

1.  Select your requests on the main table view.
    
2.  Right-Click -> Tools -> Add to Diff pool (Or using ⌘Y)
    
3.  On the Diff window, select Left and Right Panel.
    
4.  Proxyman performs the diff operation and displays it.
    

#### 

[](https://docs.proxyman.com/advanced-features/diff#side-by-side-mode)

Side-by-Side mode

![](https://docs.proxyman.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F1856518738-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252F-LlPt_6BePnJ3oK3saP1%252Fuploads%252F8EScHubheb71QvKA8L0A%252FScreen%2520Shot%25202022-03-27%2520at%252009.30.03.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3De824bef6-f357-46c6-986e-a874f5f16e76&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=95bbec1a&sv=2)

Side By Side Mode

#### 

[](https://docs.proxyman.com/advanced-features/diff#unified-mode)

Unified Mode

![](https://docs.proxyman.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F1856518738-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252F-LlPt_6BePnJ3oK3saP1%252Fuploads%252Fnnud51Dmklg6gNuUYFY5%252FScreen%2520Shot%25202022-03-27%2520at%252009.31.53.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Dd85f3fd1-1517-4fb6-8097-d00fcdf8d08c&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=1dd28310&sv=2)

Unified Mode

### 

[](https://docs.proxyman.com/advanced-features/diff#id-3.-open-with-3rd-party-diff-tools)

3\. Open with 3rd-party diff tools

*   File Merge: Required Xcode to install
    
*   Kaleidoscope: You have to install the `ksdiff` in the Kaleidoscope's preference.
    

[PreviousCode Generator](https://docs.proxyman.com/advanced-features/code-generator)
[NextAccess Control](https://docs.proxyman.com/advanced-features/access-control)

Last updated 1 year ago

# External Proxy | Proxyman

### 

[](https://docs.proxyman.com/advanced-features/external-proxy#id-1.-whats-it)

1\. What's it?

Some companies have a central Proxy server, and all outgoing requests must go through to the Proxy Server in order to access the Internet.

In this case, you might have to config Proxyman to proxy all connections to the External Proxy.

### 

[](https://docs.proxyman.com/advanced-features/external-proxy#id-2.-benefits)

2\. Benefits

*   Navigate all traffic to your cooperated Proxy Server.
    
*   Able to define Hosts, or Domains which bypass the External Proxy.
    
*   Support HTTP/HTTPS/SOCKS Proxy.
    
*   Support PAC Proxy (Automatic Proxy Configuration) (Proxyman 3.2.0+)
    

### 

[](https://docs.proxyman.com/advanced-features/external-proxy#id-3.-how-to-use)

3\. How to use

*   **Tool** menu -> **Proxy Setting** -> **External Proxy Setting...**
    
*   You can config **HTTP, HTTPS, or SOCKS Proxy**, which point to your external Proxy server.
    
*   If you have a **PAC URL**, you can use it in Automatic Proxy Configuration.
    
*   Proxyman also supports **Basic Authentication**.
    

![](https://docs.proxyman.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F1856518738-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252F-LlPt_6BePnJ3oK3saP1%252Fuploads%252FhiZM2a3fBvoxkyT7GMqO%252FScreen%2520Shot%25202022-02-24%2520at%252011.39.19.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Deb9ad47e-2da9-4481-b7cb-a068449777b2&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=a83efdf9&sv=2)

HTTP, HTTPS, SOCKS, PAC Proxy

External SOCKS Proxy with authentication is not supported.

### 

[](https://docs.proxyman.com/advanced-features/external-proxy#id-4.-bypass-proxy)

4\. Bypass Proxy

*   You can define hosts/domains that will be bypass the external proxy. Each host must be separated by a Comma. Wildcard (\* or ?) is supported.
    
*   By default, Proxyam automatically bypasses all localhost traffic from the external proxy. To enable it, please check the **"Always bypass external proxies for localhost" checkbox.**
    

Localhost traffic is traffic from your localhost, 127.0.0.1, or 0.0.0.0 with all ports.

[PreviousMap Remote](https://docs.proxyman.com/advanced-features/map-remote)
[NextSave Session](https://docs.proxyman.com/advanced-features/save-session)

Last updated 3 years ago

*   [1\. What's it?](https://docs.proxyman.com/advanced-features/external-proxy#id-1.-whats-it)
    
*   [2\. Benefits](https://docs.proxyman.com/advanced-features/external-proxy#id-2.-benefits)
    
*   [3\. How to use](https://docs.proxyman.com/advanced-features/external-proxy#id-3.-how-to-use)
    
*   [4\. Bypass Proxy](https://docs.proxyman.com/advanced-features/external-proxy#id-4.-bypass-proxy)

# Swagger OpenAPI | Proxyman

[](https://docs.proxyman.com/advanced-features/swagger-openapi#id-1.-openapi)

1\. OpenAPI


----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

From Proxyman v5.14.0 or later, Proxyman can export Proxyman Requests/Responses to OpenAPI YAML format or HTML.

*   Support YAML Format
    
*   Support HTML - Swagger OpenAPI style
    
*   Built-in in Proxyman, no need for any external dependencies.
    

![](https://docs.proxyman.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F1856518738-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252F-LlPt_6BePnJ3oK3saP1%252Fuploads%252FuIwXTP1oY4lpEJAOpvKD%252FScreenshot%25202025-01-06%2520at%25202.37.25%25E2%2580%25AFPM.jpg%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3De4ac610d-d3d6-495e-97ea-7c178d706b62&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=7b00b0af&sv=2)

Export your requests/response to OpenAPI HTML Style

[](https://docs.proxyman.com/advanced-features/swagger-openapi#id-2.-how-to-use)

2\. How to use


----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

1.  Capture HTTPS requests with Proxyman. Follow the following setup guide:
    

*   [iOS devices (iPhone, iPad)](https://docs.proxyman.com/debug-devices/ios-device)
    
*   [iOS Simulator](https://docs.proxyman.com/debug-devices/ios-simulator)
    
*   [Android devices](https://docs.proxyman.com/debug-devices/android-device#id-1.-android-setup-guide)
    
*   [Android Emulator](https://docs.proxyman.com/debug-devices/android-device/automatic-script-for-android-emulator)
    
*   [macOS (Web Browser)](https://docs.proxyman.com/debug-devices/macos)
    

Verify Proxyman can capture & decrypt your HTTPS Requests/Responses

![](https://docs.proxyman.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F1856518738-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252F-LlPt_6BePnJ3oK3saP1%252Fuploads%252FvKbt9lt4ApOXy6sUbsX3%252FCleanShot%25202025-01-06%2520at%25202%25E2%2580%25AF.47.34%25402x.jpg%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Da7fbb70f-d279-4879-8710-0a6b5262896d&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=9590bff5&sv=2)

Capture your HTTPS Request/Response

1.  Select your requests on the main table -> Right-Click -> Export -> OpenAPI -> Select either OpenAPI YAML or OpenAPI HTML
    
2.  Done ✅
    

[PreviousSOCKS Proxy](https://docs.proxyman.com/advanced-features/socks-proxy)
[NextTLS Key Logging](https://docs.proxyman.com/advanced-features/tls-key-logging)

# SOCKS Proxy | Proxyman

[](https://docs.proxyman.com/advanced-features/socks-proxy#id-1.-whats-it)

1\. What's it?


----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

From Proxyman 4.9.0, Proxyman supports SOCKS Proxy beside the normal HTTP/HTTPS Proxy.

*   Support HTTPS over SOCKS Proxy: All debugging tools (e.g. Map Local, Breakpoint, ...) still work fine.
    
*   Compatible with SOCKS 5
    

Proxyman app doesn't automatically override the System SOCKS Proxy Setting at launch time. You have to manually enable it if needed.

Proxyman only supports \`connect `` and `udp` command. The`bind` ``command is not supported yet.

[](https://docs.proxyman.com/advanced-features/socks-proxy#id-2.-how-to-use-it)

2\. How to use it?


-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

1.  Open the SOCKS Proxy Setting in Tools Menu -> Proxy Setting -> SOCKS Proxy Setting
    
2.  By default, Proxyman listens on port 8889
    
3.  On your client: Set the SOCKS proxy to 127.0.0.1 at port 8889
    

![](https://docs.proxyman.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F1856518738-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252F-LlPt_6BePnJ3oK3saP1%252Fuploads%252FrEFmycrGx972YBsFJUfT%252F252151302-d68e2a24-1310-4764-b8b5-ecc37ef42fab.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D6cb2aa47-d0dd-438e-b10b-1d8179760d87&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=732ac63a&sv=2)

SOCKS Proxy

[PreviousDNS Spoofing](https://docs.proxyman.com/advanced-features/dns-spoofing)
[NextSwagger OpenAPI](https://docs.proxyman.com/advanced-features/swagger-openapi)

# *.local requests do not appear on Proxyman | Proxyman

### 

[](https://docs.proxyman.com/troubleshooting/.local-doesnt-appear-in-proxyman#id-1.-problem)

1\. Problem

*   All requests are presented on Proxyman properly, except for some local requests (`*.local` or `localhost`)
    

### 

[](https://docs.proxyman.com/troubleshooting/.local-doesnt-appear-in-proxyman#id-2.-solution)

2\. Solution

*   If it's `localhost` request, please read the following pages
    

[I could not see any requests from my localhost server](https://docs.proxyman.com/troubleshooting/couldnt-see-any-request-from-localhost-server)

*   If it's `*.local` request:
    

Open **System Preference** -> **Network** -> **Wifi** -> **Proxies** tab -> Remove `*.local` in the Bypass List in both Web Proxy (HTTP) and Secure Web Proxy (HTTPS)

![](https://docs.proxyman.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F1856518738-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-legacy-files%2Fo%2Fassets%252F-LlPt_6BePnJ3oK3saP1%252F-M5oKxx6OZSVyP-hEc7G%252F-M5oM64S9mIFkXKI1EHP%252FScreen_Shot_2020-04-26_at_09_40_48.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D563fe662-8ed9-4f78-b564-ccd95cde756c&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=4322d3ed&sv=2)

# Custom Filters | Proxyman

[](https://docs.proxyman.com/advanced-features/custom-filters#id-1.-whats-it)

1\. What's it?


-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

From Proxyman 4.11.0 or later, users can create a filter to save current filter configs and access it later.

*   Able to create a custom Filter button on the Toolbar with the current filter config
    
*   Manage the filter buttons: Create new, Override, Delete, and Rename.
    
*   Save time ✅
    

[](https://docs.proxyman.com/advanced-features/custom-filters#id-2.-how-to-use)

2\. How to use


---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

#### 

[](https://docs.proxyman.com/advanced-features/custom-filters#create-new-filter)

Create new filter

1.  Setup your filter config (Support Single or Multiple filters)
    
2.  Click on the Save button -> Save -> Enter the name
    
3.  A New Filter is added to the Filter Toolbar.
    

![](https://docs.proxyman.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F1856518738-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252F-LlPt_6BePnJ3oK3saP1%252Fuploads%252Fyx2c3gZS3P33ff8JatAO%252FCleanShot%25202023-09-12%2520at%252010.14.31%25402x.jpg%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Dc9a8fd95-fbed-42c8-8bc3-d7ad9c28e3a8&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=527a024b&sv=2)

Create new custom filter

#### 

[](https://docs.proxyman.com/advanced-features/custom-filters#override)

Override

1.  Change your filter config
    
2.  Save button -> Override -> Select the filter that you'd like to override

Override current filter

#### 

[](https://docs.proxyman.com/advanced-features/custom-filters#delete-or-rename)

Delete or Rename

2.  Delete or Rename

# Lost data after updating Proxyman app? | Proxyman

### 

[](https://docs.proxyman.com/troubleshooting/lost-data-after-updating-proxyman-app#problem)

Problem

After updating the app to the latest version, you might encounter:

*   Your current data, including all debugging tools rules (Map Local, Scripting, Breakpoint, SSL Proxying List, ...) and user settings, etc are wiped out.
    

Proxyman will **guarantee** that your current data **is never lost**. However, it's still better if we have the backup of your valuable data ⚡️.

### 

[](https://docs.proxyman.com/troubleshooting/lost-data-after-updating-proxyman-app#how-to-recover)

How to recover

1.  Open the backup folder at `~/Library/Application Support/com.proxyman.NSProxy/user-data-backups`
    
2.  Unzip the latest backup file (You can sort by the "Add Date" in the Finder app. It will show the latest backup).
    
3.  Copy each folder of the backup folder to the app folder at `~/Library/Application Support/com.proxyman.NSProxy`
    

For instance:

Copy From

Copy To

~/Library/Application Support/com.proxyman.NSProxy/user-data-backups/userdata\_proxyman\_3.6.0\_05-24-2022-11-55-20/user-data

~/Library/Application Support/com.proxyman.NSProxy/user-data

~/Library/Application Support/com.proxyman.NSProxy/user-data-backups/userdata\_proxyman\_3.6.0\_05-24-2022-11-55-20/map-local

~/Library/Application Support/com.proxyman.NSProxy/map-local

and more...

### 

[](https://docs.proxyman.com/troubleshooting/lost-data-after-updating-proxyman-app#when-does-proxyman-backup-my-data)

When does Proxyman backup my data?

After you update Proxyman to a newer version, Proxyman might backup your current data and save at `~/Library/Application Support/com.proxyman.NSProxy/user-data-backups`

[PreviousCould not change Proxyman App Icons](https://docs.proxyman.com/troubleshooting/could-not-change-proxyman-app-icons)
[NextProxyman consumes too much RAM & unresponsive](https://docs.proxyman.com/troubleshooting/proxyman-consumes-too-much-ram-and-unresponsive)

Last updated 1 year ago

*   [Problem](https://docs.proxyman.com/troubleshooting/lost-data-after-updating-proxyman-app#problem)
    
*   [How to recover](https://docs.proxyman.com/troubleshooting/lost-data-after-updating-proxyman-app#how-to-recover)
    
*   [When does Proxyman backup my data?](https://docs.proxyman.com/troubleshooting/lost-data-after-updating-proxyman-app#when-does-proxyman-backup-my-data)

# Could not change Proxyman App Icons | Proxyman

### 

[](https://docs.proxyman.com/troubleshooting/could-not-change-proxyman-app-icons#id-1.-problems)

1\. Problems?

Proxyman 3.2.0 introduces various new App Icons that help Proxyman to be distinguished from other apps in the Dock.

If you've encountered the following issue:

*   Could not update the icon in Preference -> Theme
    

### 

[](https://docs.proxyman.com/troubleshooting/could-not-change-proxyman-app-icons#id-2.-solution)

2\. Solution

1.  Quit Proxyman -> Open Activity Monitor
    
2.  Search "Dock" in the Search Bar
    
3.  Select Dock Extra and Kill it.
    
4.  Relaunch Proxyman and select your favorite App Icon
    

![](https://docs.proxyman.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F1856518738-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252F-LlPt_6BePnJ3oK3saP1%252Fuploads%252FF7YBdj7Sne9qekJ9MMD9%252FScreen_Shot_2022-03-05_at_15_07_41.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D56a84cc3-a55f-4d9b-9ab6-96ef7d0baae6&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=40df7652&sv=2)

# Install Certificate | Proxyman

[](https://docs.proxyman.com/proxyman-windows/install-certificate#install-certificates-on-windows)

Install Certificates on Windows


---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

In order to intercept encrypted HTTPS messages (Request or Response), you have to install **Proxyman CA Certificate** on your current Windows Machine.

You can install the Proxyman CA Certificate by navigating to

*   **Certificate** menu -> **Install Certificate on this Windows**...
    

The Proxyman Certificate is a self-signed certificate, which is generated on your machine. Proxyman never stores or transmits any personal data to Proxyman's server or 3rd-party.

Please check out the [Privacy Statement](https://proxyman.io/privacy)
 to understand what Proxyman obtains or not.

If you'd like to manually generate a Certificate on your machine then adding to Proxyman. Please check out the [Custom Certificate Doc](https://docs.proxyman.com/advanced-features/custom-certificates#6-how-to-generate-self-signed-certificates-for-custom-root-certificate-that-comply-with-new-apples-security-requirements)

[](https://docs.proxyman.com/proxyman-windows/install-certificate#id-1.-automatic-mode)

1\. Automatic mode


---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

![](https://docs.proxyman.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F1856518738-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252F-LlPt_6BePnJ3oK3saP1%252Fuploads%252FB74UyKOnOUY4V92iOfaI%252FScreenshot%25202023-01-23%2520at%252009.38.09.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D9ab1da42-452a-4e95-a9cc-355661bb5cb5&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=67642c56&sv=2)

Auto install the certificate on Windows machine

Proxyman provides an automatic script to Install & Trust the Proxyman CA Certificate to the System.

*   Certificate Menu -> Install Certificate for this Windows -> Click on the "Install & Trust" button
    
*   Click YES on the System Prompt
    

![](https://docs.proxyman.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F1856518738-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252F-LlPt_6BePnJ3oK3saP1%252Fuploads%252FDmMaTE3OEbwqHIBUsOIX%252FScreenshot_2023-01-23_at_09_41_41.jpg%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Dd6455c8c-6ade-4f7a-be5a-9f2b53874e26&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=51ab3ab&sv=2)

Grant permission to run the Automatic Script

### 

[](https://docs.proxyman.com/proxyman-windows/install-certificate#why-do-i-need-to-grant-permission)

Why do I need to grant permission?

Behind the scene, Proxyman would execute the following command with Admin Mode:

[certutil](https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/windows-server/administration/windows-commands/certutil)
 is a built-in Windows command line to manage the certificate.

[](https://docs.proxyman.com/proxyman-windows/install-certificate#id-2.-manual-mode)

2\. Manual Mode


---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

If you don't have permission to execute the script, please do the following step:

1.  Close Proxyman
    
2.  Find a Proxyman CA Certificate at "C:\\Users\\<your\_username>\\AppData\\Roaming\\Proxyman\\certificate\\certs\\ca.cer"
    
3.  Double-click to open it
    
4.  Install Certificate -> Select "Current User" -> Select "Place all certificates in the following store" -> "Browse..."
    

![](https://docs.proxyman.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F1856518738-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252F-LlPt_6BePnJ3oK3saP1%252Fuploads%252FjuLJgvdX3SlydNfR7sK9%252F212792551-e3875685-294b-46b4-b563-b3c7051fb29a.jpg%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Dd4a17f38-7322-43ce-972e-f63f872aa087&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=f171d53f&sv=2)

Steps to install the certificate

5\. Select Next -> Finish

6\. Select "YES" on the System Prompt.

[PreviousTLS Key Logging](https://docs.proxyman.com/advanced-features/tls-key-logging)
[NextWSL](https://docs.proxyman.com/proxyman-windows/wsl)

Last updated 1 year ago

*   [Install Certificates on Windows](https://docs.proxyman.com/proxyman-windows/install-certificate#install-certificates-on-windows)
    
*   [1\. Automatic mode](https://docs.proxyman.com/proxyman-windows/install-certificate#id-1.-automatic-mode)

Copy

    $ certutil -addstore "Root" <Certificate_Path>

# Proxyman consumes too much RAM & unresponsive | Proxyman

[](https://docs.proxyman.com/troubleshooting/proxyman-consumes-too-much-ram-and-unresponsive#problems)

Problems


--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

If Proxyman is:

*   Unresponsive after using it for a while.
    
*   Consume too much Memory.
    

You might encounter the above problems if you enable SSL Proxying with the following rules:

*   Use the all \`\*\` wildcard to intercept all traffic from your Mac Machine.
    
*   Enable the entire web browser (Google Chrome, Safari, Firefox, etc.).
    

[](https://docs.proxyman.com/troubleshooting/proxyman-consumes-too-much-ram-and-unresponsive#reason)

**Reason**


--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Proxyman will intercept and decrypt all traffic which leads to high memory usage. In the worst scenario, the app can become unresponsive.

![](https://docs.proxyman.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F1856518738-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252F-LlPt_6BePnJ3oK3saP1%252Fuploads%252FQG6Gb8p4TKIBY3Q30b3l%252FScreen_Shot_2022-08-10_at_14_01_16.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3De0903e7a-5bfe-419d-a9cf-cc58b893670c&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=800011a2&sv=2)

SSL Proxying List with web browser or \* wildcard can slow your Mac.

[](https://docs.proxyman.com/troubleshooting/proxyman-consumes-too-much-ram-and-unresponsive#solution)

Solution


--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

1.  ✅ Update to the latest Proxyman version (Memory Leaks has been fixed in the latest builds)
    
2.  Open Tools -> SSL Proxying List
    
3.  Remove all Web Browser or \`\*\` wildcards if they exist.
    
4.  Enable SSL Proxying on particular domains.
    

[PreviousLost data after updating Proxyman app?](https://docs.proxyman.com/troubleshooting/lost-data-after-updating-proxyman-app)

Last updated 1 year ago

*   [Problems](https://docs.proxyman.com/troubleshooting/proxyman-consumes-too-much-ram-and-unresponsive#problems)
    
*   [Reason](https://docs.proxyman.com/troubleshooting/proxyman-consumes-too-much-ram-and-unresponsive#reason)
    
*   [Solution](https://docs.proxyman.com/troubleshooting/proxyman-consumes-too-much-ram-and-unresponsive#solution)

# Write your own Addons | Proxyman

[](https://docs.proxyman.com/scripting/write-your-own-addons#id-1.-whats-it)

1\. What's it?


------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

You can write your own Addon to achieve what Proxyman hasn't provided yet. You can do:

*   Write your own Javascript Addon.
    
*   Use [Built-in Libraries](https://docs.proxyman.com/scripting/built-in-js-libraries)
    .
    
*   Write your library and share it with your colleauges.
    

[](https://docs.proxyman.com/scripting/write-your-own-addons#id-2.-how-to-write-an-addon)

2\. How to write an addon?


-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

1.  Open User Addon folder at `~/Library/Application\ Support/com.proxyman.NSProxy/users` or you can open by opening the More Button -> Documentations -> Open Custom Addons Folder...
    

![](https://docs.proxyman.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F1856518738-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-legacy-files%2Fo%2Fassets%252F-LlPt_6BePnJ3oK3saP1%252F-MgziXuEudQDPNF3CBS_%252F-MgzivyyrfR93vyj9hMZ%252FScreen%2520Shot%25202021-08-13%2520at%252020.37.39.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D2a834f02-f339-422c-80ad-b5520713e876&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=e5848f45&sv=2)

2\. Duplicate `HelloWorld.js` file and rename it to **MyAwesomeAddon.js**

3\. Open the file and you can see the template.

4\. Change the metadata and write your JS Code

*   You can import built-in addons by using **require(@"addons/<name.js>")**
    

Check out the [built-in addons](https://docs.proxyman.com/scripting/addons#2-built-in-addons)
 that Proxyman provides

*   You can import a built-in library by using **require(@"lib/<name.js>")**
    

Check out the [built-in library](https://docs.proxyman.com/scripting/built-in-js-libraries)
 that Proxyman provides

5\. Save the file

6\. Open your Script in Proxyman app and import the script

**require("@users/MyAwesomeAddon.js")** is your addon directory

@users is the Custom Addons Folder.

[](https://docs.proxyman.com/scripting/write-your-own-addons#id-3.-note)

3\. Note


--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Your own scripts are stored at **~/Library/Application\\ Support/com.proxyman.NSProxy/users**

This folder is safe. It's never overridden or removed by Proxyman.

[PreviousBuilt-in JS Libraries](https://docs.proxyman.com/scripting/built-in-js-libraries)
[NextSnippet Code](https://docs.proxyman.com/scripting/snippet-code)

Last updated 4 years ago

*   [1\. What's it?](https://docs.proxyman.com/scripting/write-your-own-addons#id-1.-whats-it)
    
*   [2\. How to write an addon?](https://docs.proxyman.com/scripting/write-your-own-addons#id-2.-how-to-write-an-addon)
    
*   [3\. Note](https://docs.proxyman.com/scripting/write-your-own-addons#id-3.-note)
    

Copy

    /**
        {
            "name":"My Awesome Addon",
            "description":"The first User Addons",
            "author":"Proxyman",
            "tags":"helloworld"
        }
    **/
    
    const { md5 } = require("@addons/MD5.js");
    
    const sayHello = () => {
      var content = "Hello World. My first custom Addon.";
      var hash = md5(content);
      return content + ". MD5 = " + hash;
    };
    
    // Make sure you export the function at the end of method
    exports.sayHello = sayHello;
    

Copy

    const { md5 } = require("@addons/MD5.js");

Copy

    // Import your addon
    // Make sure you imports the function that you exports in the addons
    const { sayHello } = require("@users/MyAwesomeAddon.js");
    
    // Usage
    sayHello();

# Allow List | Proxyman

[](https://docs.proxyman.com/advanced-features/whitelist#id-1.-whats-it)

1\. What's it?


--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The Allow List Tool is a handy tool to help you define which domains you **allow to appear** on the Proxyman app.

The unmatched requests won't go through Proxyman (by-pass)

It's useful in the following situations:

*   Ignore all domains except your debugging domains (e.g. producthunt.com)
    
*   Reduce the number of unnecessary requests, and focus on the domains you need to track
    

If you would like to block certain domains, please visit [Block Tool](https://docs.proxyman.com/advanced-features/blacklist)

[](https://docs.proxyman.com/advanced-features/whitelist#id-2.-how-to-use)

2\. How to use?


-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

*   **Tools** menu -> **Allow List**
    
*   Right-click on the selected request -> **Tools** -> **Allow List**
    

![](https://docs.proxyman.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F1856518738-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-legacy-files%2Fo%2Fassets%252F-LlPt_6BePnJ3oK3saP1%252F-M9vMHE6bDvuRRohvya7%252F-M9vMwKLNrpxZ9PLmi7O%252FScreen%2520Shot%25202020-06-16%2520at%252011.24.12.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D3acc7dc2-b9d1-4f73-b1f6-1e8700f027e4&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=e2d0f1c6&sv=2)

**⌥⌘\]** to quickly open the Allow List Window

[PreviousBlock List](https://docs.proxyman.com/advanced-features/blacklist)
[NextCharles Proxy Converter](https://docs.proxyman.com/advanced-features/charles-proxy-converter)

Last updated 3 months ago

*   [1\. What's it?](https://docs.proxyman.com/advanced-features/whitelist#id-1.-whats-it)

# I could not see any HTTP traffic from my NodeJS, Python, or Ruby scripts | Proxyman

[](https://docs.proxyman.com/troubleshooting/i-could-not-see-any-http-traffic-from-my-nodejs-python-or-ruby-scripts#id-1.-problem)

1\. Problem:


----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

*   I have NodeJS, Ruby, Python, or Golang scripts/servers, which make an internal HTTP/HTTPS request -> However, I don't see any traffic from the Proxyman app.
    

For example:

*   NodeJS: I'm using the [axios](https://github.com/axios/axios)
     library (NodeJS) to call a RESTFUL API from my production server (e.g. https://mycompany.com/v1/data). However, there is no traffic recorded from the Proxyman app.
    
*   I'm using net/http from Golang, but no requests appear on Proxyman
    
*   ... so all
    

[](https://docs.proxyman.com/troubleshooting/i-could-not-see-any-http-traffic-from-my-nodejs-python-or-ruby-scripts#id-2.-new-automatic-solution-v4.7.0-or-later)

2\. New Automatic Solution (v4.7.0 or later) ✅


---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Proxyman v4.7.0 or later can capture HTTP/HTTPS traffic from Python/Ruby/NodeJS/Golang with 1-click.

*   1-click solution: No need to manually set HTTP Proxy config or trust the self-signed certificate.
    
*   Support many network libraries from NodeJS, Python, Ruby, and Golang
    

### 

[](https://docs.proxyman.com/troubleshooting/i-could-not-see-any-http-traffic-from-my-nodejs-python-or-ruby-scripts#id-2.1-how-to-use)

2.1 How to use:

1.  Open Proxyman -> Setup Menu -> Automatic Setup
    
2.  Click on "Open New Terminal"
    

![](https://docs.proxyman.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F1856518738-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252F-LlPt_6BePnJ3oK3saP1%252Fuploads%252F4CIEVKhzglYi5T3YHVLT%252FScreenshot%25202025-03-18%2520at%252010.54.37.jpg%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D295c1e9f-10ce-4766-ab65-e08d24f79858&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=609f0abc&sv=2)

Start pre-configured Terminal

1.  Accept the Apple Script permission prompt if needed
    
2.  The New Terminal app is launched -> You can start your Python Backend Server, or Run scripts => Proxyman automatically captures all traffic.
    

![](https://docs.proxyman.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F1856518738-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252F-LlPt_6BePnJ3oK3saP1%252Fuploads%252FtsBq8JdHXuQU1vL31PYZ%252FCleanShot%25202025-03-18%2520at%252009.56.44%25402x.jpg%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Ddf25804a-c39b-4c87-9422-b52ab338b7a3&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=ed38baa2&sv=2)

Capture HTTPS traffic from Ruby, Python, NodeJS and Golang Server/Scripts

1.  Done ✅
    

[](https://docs.proxyman.com/troubleshooting/i-could-not-see-any-http-traffic-from-my-nodejs-python-or-ruby-scripts#id-3.-other-problems)

# WSL | Proxyman

### 

[](https://docs.proxyman.com/proxyman-windows/wsl#id-1.-whats-it)

1\. What's it?

In order to use Automatic Script for Android Emulator, the following command line must be installed on your Windows machine:

*   wsl
    
*   choco (package manager for Windows)
    
*   adb (Android Debug Bridge)
    

### 

[](https://docs.proxyman.com/proxyman-windows/wsl#id-2.-install-wsl-on-windows-10-11)

2\. Install WSL on Windows 10/11

1.  On Windows 10/11, search: **Command Prompt** app
    
2.  Right-click on the app -> Select **Run as administrator** option.
    
3.  When the App is opened, copy & paste the following command:
    

Copy

    wsl --install

1.  Restart your Windows to take effect -> After restarting, Windows will open the **Command Prompt** which asks the user to create a new Username / Password -> Follow this instruction
    
2.  Open the Command Prompt app again, execute:
    

Copy

    wsl

1.  Verify that the command is successful, with no errors:
    

![](https://docs.proxyman.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F1856518738-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252F-LlPt_6BePnJ3oK3saP1%252Fuploads%252F0KiuitXtLhZlLyIGq2SI%252FCleanShot%25202024-03-29%2520at%25209%25E2%2580%25AF.43.29%25402x.jpg%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Ddb043567-0163-4af1-82d7-725f608c7eeb&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=7fde5e91&sv=2)

1.  Done ✅
    

### 

[](https://docs.proxyman.com/proxyman-windows/wsl#id-2.-install-choco-on-windows-10-11)

2\. Install **Choco** on Windows 10/11

1.  Open PowerShell with Run as Administrator
    
2.  Paste and run it:
    

1.  Wait a few seconds for the command to complete.
    
2.  If you don't see any errors, you are ready to use Chocolatey! Type choco or choco -? now, or see Getting Started for usage instructions.
    

Choco Installation Guide: [https://chocolatey.org/install#individual](https://chocolatey.org/install#individual)

### 

[](https://docs.proxyman.com/proxyman-windows/wsl#id-3.-install-adb-on-windows-10-11)

3\. Install **adb** on Windows 10/11

1.  Open PowerShell with Run as Administrator
    
2.  Run:
    

1.  Verify the **adb** is successfully installed and there is no error
    

### 

[](https://docs.proxyman.com/proxyman-windows/wsl#id-4.-done.-try-to-use-android-automatic-script-again-on-proxyman-app)

4\. ✅ Done. Try to Use Android Automatic Script again on Proxyman app

### 

[](https://docs.proxyman.com/proxyman-windows/wsl#id-5.-references)

5\. References:

Copy

    Set-ExecutionPolicy Bypass -Scope Process -Force; [System.Net.ServicePointManager]::SecurityProtocol = [System.Net.ServicePointManager]::SecurityProtocol -bor 3072; iex ((New-Object System.Net.WebClient).DownloadString('https://community.chocolatey.org/install.ps1'))

Copy

    choco install adb -y

# Custom Certificates | Proxyman

### 

[](https://docs.proxyman.com/advanced-features/custom-certificates#id-1.-whats-it)

1\. What's it?

Proxyman supports Custom **Root Certificate**, **Server Certificates, and** **Client Certificates** that allow you to add your certificate that Proxyman uses to establish the SSL-Connection between your clients, servers, and Proxyman app.

Custom Certificate Type

Purpose

How Proxyman uses

**Server Certificate**

For intercepting HTTPS Traffic from clients that use SSL-Pinning

Use this certificate for SSL-Handshake to your Clients

**Client Certificate**

For intercepting HTTPS Traffic from clients that use Mutual Authentication

Use this certificate for SSL-Handshake to specific Server

**Root Certificate**

For intercepting HTTPS Traffic from clients and servers without using local Proxyman certificates

SSL Handshake for both clients & servers

![](https://docs.proxyman.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F1856518738-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-legacy-files%2Fo%2Fassets%252F-LlPt_6BePnJ3oK3saP1%252F-MGm2WFKbZjCmxjt4i5S%252F-MGm3TcUSUGtWQX56SNO%252FScreen%2520Shot%25202020-09-09%2520at%252015.52.42.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Dae9f847b-5f4d-4849-9dc1-4b5e9eaef3b7&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=dc7b4fc7&sv=2)

Even though the Proxyman Root Certificate is locally generated in your machine, you can manually generate and add to Proxyman. [Read more](https://docs.proxyman.com/advanced-features/custom-certificates#6-how-to-generate-self-signed-certificates-that-meet-apples-requirements)

### 

[](https://docs.proxyman.com/advanced-features/custom-certificates#id-2.-certificate-formats)

2\. Certificate Formats

Proxyman accepts the following formats:

Custom Certificate

PEM or DER

PKCS #12 (p12)

Root Certificate

Not Supported

Supported

Client Certificate

Supported

Supported

Server Certificate

Supported

Supported

*   PKCS #12 (p12).
    
*   PEM or DER Private Key and Certificate file.
    

*   Proxyman automatically determines the format of the Private Key and Certificate file (Support PEM or DER).
    
*   Proxyman will prompt to enter the password if import an encrypted Private Key or PKCS #12 file.
    
*   All passphrases are securely stored in Proxyman Keychain.
    

If your certificates are in different formats that Proxyman supports, please convert them to p12 or PEM/DER format before importing.

### 

[](https://docs.proxyman.com/advanced-features/custom-certificates#id-3.-certificate-requirement-on-macos-10.15-and-ios-13)

3\. Certificate Requirement on macOS 10.15+ and iOS 13+

If you're using a custom Root Certificate or Server Certificate on macOS 10.15 or iOS 13, you might encounter the failed handshake on Safari or iOS devices if the following requirements don't meet:

*   RSA Key must have a key size is greater than 2048 bits
    
*   The hash algorithm is SHA-2 family
    
*   DNS Name of the server must be present on Subject Alternative Name. Common Name is no longer trusted
    
*   Valid certificate (Current day is in Not Before and Not After)
    
*   TLS server certificates must contain an ExtendedKeyUsage (EKU) extension containing the **id-kp-serverAuth** OID.
    

Read more [https://support.apple.com/en-us/HT210176](https://support.apple.com/en-us/HT210176)

If it's too complicated for you, we recommend letting Proxyman performs it automatically. Please visit Certificate Menu -> Install Certificate on this Mac -> Select **Automatic** Tab.

### 

[](https://docs.proxyman.com/advanced-features/custom-certificates#id-4.-common-issues)

4\. Common issues

Problem

Solution

Private Key and Certificate are not matched

Try different certificates and private keys and make sure they are matched

Get SSL Handshake Error for custom certificates

*   Try to add the custom Certificate to System Keychain and Trust it
    
*   Certificate doesn't match the requirement from macOS => Read [section 3](https://docs.proxyman.com/advanced-features/custom-certificates#3-certificate-requirement-on-macos-10-15-and-ios-13)
    
*   Check expires day of the Certificate
    

Could not import certificate due to invalid passphrase

Ask your leader to give the correct passphrase to open the encrypted Private Key or P12 file

### 

[](https://docs.proxyman.com/advanced-features/custom-certificates#id-5.-how-to-use)

5\. How to use

*   Access from **Certificate Menu** -> **Add Custom Certificate**
    

![](https://docs.proxyman.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F1856518738-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-legacy-files%2Fo%2Fassets%252F-LlPt_6BePnJ3oK3saP1%252F-MfwiNzMSsWbrhIP0uXH%252F-MfwibXWpHoYDNlEzUpL%252FScreen%2520Shot%25202021-07-31%2520at%252020.21.35.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D1fb90e47-c093-4d36-9693-2653bd128811&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=1791f85b&sv=2)

### 

[](https://docs.proxyman.com/advanced-features/custom-certificates#id-6.-how-to-generate-self-signed-certificates-for-custom-root-certificate-that-comply-with-new-apples)

**6\. How to generate self-signed certificates for Custom Root Certificate that comply with new Apple's Security Requirements**

Due to [Apple's requirements from iOS 13 and Catalina (10.15)](https://docs.proxyman.com/advanced-features/custom-certificates#3-certificate-requirement-on-macos-10-15-and-ios-13)
, It requires extra configuration to generate the self-signed certificate properly.

The following steps will guide you on how to do it properly:

1.  Prepare a `cert.config` file on the **Desktop folder**
    

*   Please update values for C, L, O, CN, and OU parameters.
    

2\. Generate RSA Key in the Terminal app. (Replace **your\_password** with any password, e.g. 123456)

3\. Generate the self-signed certificate and private key. (Replace **your\_password** with the password in step 2)

4\. Convert to p12 format. (Replace **your\_password** with the password in step 2)

5\. Finally, you would have **root-ca.p12** file and move to the next step

If you can't import your custom certificate on macOS 14 (OpenSSL v3) or later, you should use the \`-legacy\` flag in step 4.

Ref: [https://stackoverflow.com/questions/70431528/mac-verification-failed-during-pkcs12-import-wrong-password-azure-devops](https://stackoverflow.com/questions/70431528/mac-verification-failed-during-pkcs12-import-wrong-password-azure-devops)

### 

[](https://docs.proxyman.com/advanced-features/custom-certificates#id-7.-import-as-a-custom-root-certificate)

7\. Import as a Custom Root Certificate

1.  Go to Certificate Menu -> Custom Certificate -> Select Root Certificate Tab
    
2.  Click **Import** button -> P12
    
3.  Select **root-ca.p12** file and enter the password.
    
4.  Trust your custom certificate in Keychain Access App:
    

*   Open Keychain Access App
    
*   Search for the certificate you've added. The name might be the common name (CN) of the certificate
    
*   Double Click to open and select Always Trust
    
*   Click "X" and save the change
    

![](https://docs.proxyman.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F1856518738-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-legacy-files%2Fo%2Fassets%252F-LlPt_6BePnJ3oK3saP1%252F-MGm4iuVt7z3J58Y_2Qd%252F-MGm7bagKptMg27z3I-B%252FScreen%2520Shot%25202020-09-09%2520at%252006.30.51.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D7e2a9620-67f1-4bbe-9e8e-51fc954474c1&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=6b41d0f2&sv=2)

5\. Please verify that you can see the Green Tick that shows the certificate is installed and trusted properly.

![](https://docs.proxyman.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F1856518738-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-legacy-files%2Fo%2Fassets%252F-LlPt_6BePnJ3oK3saP1%252F-MGnAtKYFECJc6-DqlVs%252F-MGnB4vOeNn-LubpeLLD%252FScreen%2520Shot%25202020-09-09%2520at%252020.52.39.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D21bee69b-c9c6-4873-a77b-b011d7e0a7cd&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=9767caef&sv=2)

Custom Root Certificate is installed and trusted properly. Ready to go!

### 

[](https://docs.proxyman.com/advanced-features/custom-certificates#id-8.-import-as-a-server-client-certificate)

8\. Import as a Server/Client Certificate

For custom Server/Client certificates, you should not generate a self-signed certificate. Please ask your workmate or team lead about the certificate that the company is using. It could be in DER/PEM or P12 format.

Then import the certificate as a Server / Client Certificate in Custom Certificate Window.

![](https://docs.proxyman.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F1856518738-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-legacy-files%2Fo%2Fassets%252F-LlPt_6BePnJ3oK3saP1%252F-MAil4GrBFa-_bEYc1Zl%252F-MAioZF7Q4lXuoCI6mKA%252FScreen%2520Shot%25202020-06-26%2520at%252010.54.35.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Dd553135e-8e19-479c-9ae4-5f7eebbdeaea&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=57dbdbb9&sv=2)

Import PEM/DER key and private key to Custom Client/Server Certificate

You don't need to trust the certificate on System Keychain since it's not a Root Certificate.

Copy

    [ ca ]
    default_ca    = CA_default
    [ CA_default ]
    default_md    = sha256
    [ v3_ca ]
    subjectKeyIdentifier=hash
    authorityKeyIdentifier=keyid:always,issuer
    basicConstraints = critical,CA:true
    keyUsage=critical,keyCertSign
    extendedKeyUsage = serverAuth,clientAuth
    [ req ]
    prompt = no
    distinguished_name    = req_distinguished_name
    [ req_distinguished_name ]
    C=US
    L=US
    O=Proxyman LLC
    CN=proxyman.dev
    OU=Proxyman

Copy

    cd ~/Desktop
    openssl genrsa -aes256 -passout pass:your_password -out key.pem 2048

Copy

    openssl req -x509 -new -nodes -passin pass:your_password -config cert.config -key key.pem -sha256 -extensions v3_ca -days 825 -out root-ca.pem

Copy

    openssl pkcs12 -export -legacy -out root-ca.p12 -in root-ca.pem -inkey key.pem -passin pass:your_password -passout pass:your_password
